## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task seeks the rate law dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t. In chemical kinetics, the rate of change of a reactant concentration typically follows power-law dependence on concentration, but complex mechanisms can introduce time-dependent terms or non-integer orders.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to concentration squared)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate dependence)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reaction with equilibrium)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (self-catalysis with linear and quadratic terms)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (saturation-type rate law, similar to enzyme kinetics)
- Second-order with time modulation: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order with constant production/removal)
- Parallel reactions: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**c2 (competing pathways with different orders)
- Time-dependent forcing: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * t (linear time-dependent source term)
- Oscillatory driving: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (periodically driven reaction)
- Power-law with time decay: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (time-dependent rate with power-law aging)
- Rational rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 / (c1 + A**2) (cooperative or inhibited kinetics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure concentration dependence (no explicit t) → classical rate law dA/dt = f(A), suggesting a closed kinetic scheme
- Linear dependence on A → first-order kinetics, exponential decay/growth solution A(t) = A0*exp(kt)
- Quadratic dependence on A → second-order kinetics, hyperbolic time dependence 1/A ~ t
- Rational function of A (A/(1+A) type) → enzyme-like or saturation kinetics with limiting rate
- Explicit time dependence in rate → non-autonomous system, possibly from eliminated intermediates or external perturbation
- Negative constant term plus positive A-dependent term → reversible reaction approaching equilibrium
- Product of A terms with different powers → parallel or competing reaction pathways
- Polynomial in A with alternating signs → complex mechanism with both production and consumption terms
- Rate proportional to A*(c0 - A) → logistic-type autocatalytic kinetics with finite capacity
- Exponential time factor multiplying concentration terms → time-varying temperature or catalyst deactivation (Arrhenius-like modulation)

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK19)

GT: -c0*A**c1 - c2*A*exp(-c3*_s*t) + c4*_t*sin(log(A + c5))
Candidate formulas: 55

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT:

**GT:** `-0.16498*A² - 0.16498*A*exp(-0.01276*t) + 0.6208*sin(log(A + 1))`

Let me analyze the structure: three terms:
1. A quadratic term: `-0.16498*A²`
2. An exponential decay term: `-0.16498*A*exp(-0.01276*t)`
3. A sinusoidal term: `0.6208*sin(log(A + 1))`

I need to find a candidate that can produce all three components.

Let me focus on candidates that have `sin(log(...))` or `cos(log(...))` terms, since the GT has `sin(log(A+1))`.

Note: `sin(log(A+1)) = cos(log(A+1) - π/2)`, so `cos(log(A+1))` with a phase shift could work, but `cos(c*log(A+1))` needs `c=1` and a phase mechanism.

**Candidates with `cos(c*log(c*|A|+1))`:** 11, 12, 16, 22, 27, 31, 33, 38, 46, 47

For these, the trig term is `c*cos(c*log(c*|A|+1))`. Since A≥0, |A|=A. We need `cos(c6*log(c7*A+1))` to equal `sin(log(A+1))`.

Using `sin(x) = cos(x - π/2)`, we need `cos(log(A+1) - π/2)`. But `cos(c6*log(c7*A+1))` has no phase shift parameter — it can only match `cos(c6*log(c7*A+1))`, not `sin(log(A+1))`.

So these can't match unless there's another mechanism. Let me look more carefully...

**Candidate 46:** `A²*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + A*c3 + c4 + c5*cos(c6*log(c7*|A|+1))`

This has terms: `A²*c0`, `A*c1*exp(c2*t)`, `A*c3`, `c4`, `c5*cos(c6*log(c7*A+1))`. No phase shift in cosine — can't match sin(log(A+1)).

**Candidate 32:** `A³*c0 + A²*c1 + A*c2*exp(c3*t) + A*c4 + c5 + c6*sin(c7*log(A²*c8+1) + c9)`

This has `sin(c7*log(c8*A²+1) + c9)`. Can this match `sin(log(A+1))`? We need `c7*log(c8*A²+1) + c9 = log(A+1)`. But `log(c8*A²+1)` vs `log(A+1)` — these are fundamentally different functions of A, so no.

Set c0=0: `A²*c1 + A*c2*exp(c3*t) + A*c4 + c5 + c6*cos(c7*log(c8*A+1))`. Still no phase shift for cosine.

**Candidate 38:** `A²*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + A*c3 + A*c4/(A+c5) + c6 + c7*cos(c8*log(c9*|A|+1))`

Set c4=0, c5 absorbed into c6. Still cos without phase.

**Candidate 11:** `A²*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + A*c3 + A*c4*t*exp(c5*t) + c6 + c7*cos(c8*log(c9*|A|+1))`

Set c4=0: `A²*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + A*c3 + c6 + c7*cos(c8*log(c9*A+1))`. Still can't get sin from cos without phase shift.

None of the candidates with `cos(c*log(...))` have a phase parameter. And none have `sin(log(A+c))` directly.

After thorough analysis, no candidate can reproduce `sin(log(A+1))` — the cos-log candidates lack phase shifts, and other candidates use different functional forms.
